Richard C. Steffens wrote:

>  I suspect the version I bought, at Car Toys, was
> made for Verizon, since I got it with a Verizon calling plan.

I don't know much about this, but I've read on several occasions that 
Verizon is notorious for locking down their phones.  Features that exist 
on a stock RAZR are not necessarily available on the Verizon RAZR, which 
is pathetic.  So what people have done is flash their Verizon phone with 
firmware from another provider.  Verizon's network is CDMA, so you'll 
need to get the RAZR firmwre from another CDMA provider, such as Alltel 
or Cricket.  Cingular/ATT and T-Mobile are GSM providers and theirs 
won't work.  You might want to research if the features you'll get give 
you what you want, but it seems many people are doing this with success. 
  This should get you started:

http://www.google.com/search?q=verizon+razr+firmware

-- 
- m0gely

Rich Shepard wrote:
> On Wed, 6 Jun 2007, Carlos Konstanski wrote:
> 
>> It appears that you are correct in presuming that BigDecimal is java's
>> way
>> of handling accounting arithmetic.  I found a Sun java API for smart card
>> programming, which contains a class called BigNumber, which encapsulates
>> BCD representation.  But it looks far too chunky to use in an accounting
>> app, while BigDecimal seems adequate for the task.
> 
> Carlos,
> 
>   I remember struggling to learn BCD for use in FORTRAN IV with the WATFOR
> compiler on main frames. Those IBM manuals were terrible!
> 
>> In a world where languages exist that can easily handle the math
>> (fortran,
>> lisp, caml), why do we use java for accounting anyway?  What a marketing
>> triumph.  Maybe we should rename lisp after an addictive beverage, and
>> then everyone will want it.  I propose "Urquell".
> 
>   Well, here's something to think about: use java for the middleware and
> front end (with SWING), but use PostgreSQL (or SQLite3) for the back end.
> They have data types (NUMERIC and DECIMAL, with postgres; INTEGER in
> sqlite)
> with sufficient precision, but you need ancillary functions to make them
> work like the deprecated MONEY type in postgres. But, storing the
> accounting
> data in tables makes present and future maintenance so much easier.
> 
>   If you want to look at a perl example for ideas, look at SQL-Ledger
> <http://www.sql-ledger.org/>. You might be able to port it from perl to
> java
> to meet your company's needs.
> 
> Rich
> 

I'll weigh in on the side of BigDecimal coming in from the Ruby world.
Decades ago there were two kinds of computers, binary for science and
decimal for business, with an occasional half-breed like the IBM 1620
being decimal for science. ;) Even interest calculations, that involve
exponentials and logarithms, can be done in BigDecimal, IIRC.

Interestingly enough, the Ruby BigDecimal library includes routines to
do linear and non-linear algebra -- LU decomposition and Newton
iterations, for example.

>      be), your program can be distributed freely, under both Linux
>      /and/ Windows (see
>      http://trolltech.com/developer/downloads/qt/windows.)

>   3. Stable and reliable: Both C++ and QT4 have been around for a long
>      time and both appear to be quite stable and reliable: both from a
>      design perspective and a QA perspective.
> 
> 
>    I also plan to draw certain design ideas from a few existing
> graphing-like applications. Namely:
> 
>    * Kivio: The front-end they use for their graphing library. It is
>      nicely done and a lot can (and should) be drawn from it.
> 
>    * Umbrello: It automates certain things about building UML diagrams.

>      (should) auto-inherit public and protected methods. These would be
>      useful generalize and allow the user to decide if and when they
>      want these automated features active (like, for example, I
>      shouldn't be forced to have aggregations going to diagram-defined
>      classes when I've specified them as attributes of a class, even if
>      it's "correct").
> 
>    * Visio: It implements custom nodes of some sort and should probably
>      be looked at.
> 
>    * PIGALE: It seems to do a lot of the stuff I'm talking about, and a
>      few concepts not really seen in most graphing programs, such as
>      multi-dimensional graphs. This should be looked into by all means.
> 
> 
>    I'm posting a notification of this here because this is my first
> major project---open source or otherwise---and I could use some advice
> from a veteran open source software developer on the logistical and
> pragmatic ends of open source development. I'm also looking for anyone
> interested in joining me in developing this graphing program. I've
> already submitted this project for consideration for hosting at
> sourceforge.net and, if all goes well, it will be approved soon. I'd
> also like feedback in general on my ideas in general. Is what I'm
> planning something others would be interested in or am I just
> reinventing the wheel?
> 
>    Thanks in advance for all your support!
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug
> 

1. A couple of other wheels that you might want to look at:

a. Dia/dia2code/tedia2sql
b. Graphviz
c. XFig

You've looked at Visio, Kivio and Pigale, which I haven't seen.

2. QT4 is an excellent toolkit and is available in open source for for
Windows, unlike its predecessors. Unless you're hell-bent on sticking
with C++, I'd recommend using a "scripting language" like Perl, Python
or Ruby, though. All of them have excellent bindings to QT4 and IIRC to
"boost" as well. And you don't have to recompile stuff to be
cross-platform -- the scripting language interpreters and run-times are
cross-platform by design.

3. KDE sorta kinda can be made to work on Windows. I have no idea about
Macs, though. By "sorta kinda can be made to work", I mean:

a. First you have to load CygWin
b. Then you have to go to the CygWin "ports" project and find a recent
version of KDE and all the libraries.
c. Then you have to start up KDE, and it's slower than the proverbial
January molasses.

In short, my recommendation is that you design at the QT4/scripting
language level and let the scripting language libraries take care of
integration with the platforms/desktops (Windows, Mac, Linux/Gnome,
Linux/KDE and Solaris)

>>
>>   Well, here's something to think about: use java for the middleware and
>> front end (with SWING), but use PostgreSQL (or SQLite3) for the back end.
>> They have data types (NUMERIC and DECIMAL, with postgres; INTEGER in
>> sqlite)

>> work like the deprecated MONEY type in postgres. But, storing the

>
> I'll weigh in on the side of BigDecimal coming in from the Ruby world.
> Decades ago there were two kinds of computers, binary for science and
> decimal for business, with an occasional half-breed like the IBM 1620
> being decimal for science. ;) Even interest calculations, that involve
> exponentials and logarithms, can be done in BigDecimal, IIRC.
>
> Interestingly enough, the Ruby BigDecimal library includes routines to
> do linear and non-linear algebra -- LU decomposition and Newton
> iterations, for example.

I've gotten some good responses on this thread.  I am constrained to
writing the app in java, due to deployment restrictions (it must run
in an Oracle Portal Application Server).  So I went with
java.math.BigDecimal.

A point was raised in this thread about how representing numbers as
strings is useful as a workaaround to the decimal rounding issue.
BigDecimal has both a double and a String constructor.  I believe that
the String constructor is supposed to guarantee that the BigDecimal
will represent the same number as the String.  This makes BigDecimal a
convenient bridge between String representation of numbers (at least
initially) and usability of the representation in arithmetic.

I've chosen a solution, but that doesn't mean I've heard enough on the
subject.  This is one of those fundamental areas of computer science
that ought to fascinate a programmer to no end.  Programmers can be
more artist than scientist, so they need to pay attention to the
science.  Finding a language that deals with the problem
satisfactorily and studying its implementation would be a good
exercise.

Carlos Konstanski


From tonyr42 at gmail.com  Sat Jun  9 20:24:43 2007
From: tonyr42 at gmail.com (Tony Rick)
Date: Sat, 9 Jun 2007 20:24:43 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] vim question
In-Reply-To: <20070606210025.62af4462@badger.had1.or.comcast.net.>
References: <20070606210025.62af4462@badger.had1.or.comcast.net.>
Message-ID: <4da3d49b0706092024n54347f4am37dabdd5fe09571e@mail.gmail.com>

It depends on what you are trying to do: learn what >> is about,  learn how
to control
indenting more, or solve a particular indenting problem?

I like syntax highlighting, syntax sensitive indenting, 4 space tab stops,
and tabs
replaced with spaces automatically.  Here's my .vimrc:

  :syn on
  set tabstop=4
  set softtabstop=4
  set shiftwidth=4
  set expandtab
  autocmd BufRead *.py set smartindent
cinwords=if,elif,else,for,while,try,except,finally,def,class

You should read up on these and try any or all of them.  The 'autocmd' is
especially interesting.
In my example, 'autocmd' applies an automatic indent after a newline
following one of the
syntax keyword phrases in Python (specified by  *.py and cinwords in the
command definition).
There is apparently a smarter indent control setting 'cindent' for c/c++
code that will indent and
unindent automatically based on syntax.  I've never tried that one, either.

>From my reading of the vim Help file, >> is a 'shift' command macro, not a
tab insert, meaning,
approximately, shift the current line 'tabstop' spaces to the right.  It can
take a number argument,
>><number>, meaning 'apply this shift command to <number> lines'.  There is
another version,
><motion>, that I have never used, but maybe it means something like 'select
some number of
lines with the mouse/cursor' (?), and apply the shift'.

- tony

From david.fleck at mchsi.com  Sun Jun 10 05:43:31 2007
From: david.fleck at mchsi.com (David Fleck)
Date: Sun, 10 Jun 2007 07:43:31 -0500 (CDT)
Subject: [PLUG] getting the latest CVS tagged version
In-Reply-To: <81629026.1181277123127.JavaMail.root@fepweb09>
References: <81629026.1181277123127.JavaMail.root@fepweb09>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0706100737090.14444@grond.sourballs.org>

On Thu, 7 Jun 2007, tkubaska at charter.net wrote:
> 1. I think I want to programmatically find out what the latest tagged 
> version in a CVS repository is. 2. I'm using an IDE (Eclipse) and I can 
> find that out pretty easily from the IDE but I don't know how to do this 
> programmatically. What I've been doing is grabbing HEAD. I always know 
> the name HEAD. But what I really want is the latest tagged version. 3. I 
> want to then build and deploy that latest version.

Does the 'latest tagged version' have a consistent name? In other words, 
do you use a specific tag that gets moved to successive file versions as 
time progresses?  If so, then checking out to that specific tag is simple.

 cvs up -r{tag_name_here}

If the tag names vary, it becomes more complex.  I'd first ask youself why 
you need to do it that way, and if there isn't some way that the 'latest 
tag' can't be made to conform to a standard such that you could check it 
out by using a constant tag name.

(You might be able to do something with grabbing the tag out of the 'cvs 
log' command for each file being updated, but that seems like a 
cumbersome, fragile and prone-to-error method; a given revision can have 
multiple tags, and the first revision in the log may not be to the latest 
version in the repository anyway.)  

--
David Fleck
david.fleck at mchsi.com

In our shop, we use the cvs -D 'date' parameter to check out code as it 
was at a particular time (usually a few minutes before the build starts).  
We generate the 'date' argument programmatically, and use a variant of it 
to identify the build packages (which are not jar files).  We log the 
'date' argument used, so that we can get back to that specific set of code 
later.  (We actually did tag every build for a while, but that became 
ridiculous.)

Can you get ant or eclipse to feed a date parameter to cvs?

> What I've (through a lot of frustration) discovered is that there does 
> not appear to be a way of breaking the connection between the name used 
> for checkout and the name used for jarring. If there is, I would be 
> thrilled to find it.
>
> The solution may turn out to be as simple as letting this automated 
> system build the way it wants to and then rename the files at the end. 
> This would probably mean deleting the generated zip file and then 
> rezipping with the renamed jar files.

Afraid I don't know enough about ant or eclipse to help here. Your problem 
sounds more and more like a limitation of the ant script (or of ant 
itself).  Your delete-and-rezip idea may be the most direct answer, even 
if it's not as clean as you'd like.

> So there are really two parts to my question. 1. Am I thinking of all 
> this in the right way ... that is, am I trying to do something 
> unconventional (I don't want to) and is there a more standard way of 
> providing daily builds to users. 

'Sticking today's date on the packagename' sounds pretty conventional to 
me.  

> And 2) if my goal is a conventional one, how do people interact with

Sorry, can't help you there. We write all our own tools for cvs

From tkubaska at charter.net  Sun Jun 10 07:56:40 2007
From: tkubaska at charter.net (Ted Kubaska)
Date: Sun, 10 Jun 2007 07:56:40 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] headless builds and automatically generated files
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0706100747020.14444@grond.sourballs.org>
References: <407983231.1181323847418.JavaMail.root@fepweb14>
	<Pine.LNX.4.63.0706100747020.14444@grond.sourballs.org>
Message-ID: <1181487400.5515.30.camel@halibut>

Thanks...most of my problem was not understanding what it was I wanted
to do. That's why I kept talking about conventions.

What we really want to do was check out the HEAD and then build and
timestamp the build without tagging the new build in the CVS repository.
Because it's just a daily build, meant to be the latest snapshot for our
users. We do tag our releases and interim releases and these are
supported. The daily build is not.

Renaming files does not work because the jar names *must* correspond to 
the Bundle-Version in the jars.

It turns out that the solution is to set the property
forceContextQualifier to the timestamp. And you can do this in the
build.properties file, which is a standard file in this headless eclipse
build environment. Or even in the ant file called by cruisecontrol as
follows (D means we're in a daily build).

<condition property="forceContextQualifier" value="${timestamp}">
  <equals arg1="${buildType}" arg2="D" />
</condition>

I hadn't known about this property ... but it's right there in the docs.
And the docs are written well enough ... there's just so much of them.

Comments below also.


On Sun, 2007-06-10 at 08:05 -0500, David Fleck wrote:

> that tag, builds it, jars it, and sticks the name of the tag into the jar 
> name?
Yes. The way the headless build environment operated was that you
checked out HEAD or a tag, built, and then either HEAD or that tagname
was incorporated into the build naming conventions. I couldn't see how
to break the connection between the tag of what we checked out and what
we built with. Well, you can see where to break that link but it's in
automatically generated files that get re-generated every time.

But there was a property that let me do this, described above.

From aledonne.listmail at gmail.com  Sun Jun 10 10:07:29 2007

Subject: [PLUG] How many ways to write a FQDN???
In-Reply-To: <1181158884.24935.0.camel@goose.robinson-west.com>
References: <1181158884.24935.0.camel@goose.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <1d065ed40706101007m78af7a06q88ba8f2034b88ed6@mail.gmail.com>

On 6/6/07, someone <plug_1 at robinson-west.com> wrote:
> How many ways can a fully qualified DNS domain name be written that
> are resolveable?
>
> I know of only this one:
>
> some.name.com
>
> Are there other possibilities that are common in SMTP email headers?
>
> On the subject, what is the maximum nth level subdomain for DNS names?
> I know it's possibly to get to 4 levels.  For example.
>
> For some.name.com, it has a first level of the root domain, a second
> level of the .com sub domain, a third level of the .name subdomain,
> and fourth level
> of the some. host name.
>
> If I know the longest name that DNS can do, that makes it potentially
> possible to avoid doing unnecessary DNS searches on bogus FQDN strings.
>
> RFC 1035 suggest 255 octets which means, I think, that a fully qualified
> domain name can have up to 255 characters in it.  Whether that includes
> the
> periods or not, I'm not sure.
>
>       Michael C. Robinson


DNS and SMTP can be odd little beasties.

As far as DNS, the number of segments is limited only by the overall
length, so a host name like:

i.want.to.send.mail.from.a.really.long.host.name.example.com

is perfectly legitimate.

One other addressing form common when dealing with SMTP:
[192.168.1.1] - literal IP in place of a host name; must be in the
square brackets

Also, DNS names may include a trailing period. It represents the root
node, and is almost always omitted.

Just a few things to keep in mind.

-Alex


From creswick at gmail.com  Sun Jun 10 11:05:54 2007
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)

Subject: [PLUG] About to start developing a new Graphing (as in

In-Reply-To: <466B004B.2040303@cesmail.net>
References: <466A40BC.7030907@yahoo.com> <466B004B.2040303@cesmail.net>
Message-ID: <c834ec80706101105r138df350w19790bad5b94eb4b@mail.gmail.com>

On 6/9/07, M. Edward (Ed) Borasky <znmeb at cesmail.net> wrote:
>
> In short, my recommendation is that you design at the QT4/scripting
> language level and let the scripting language libraries take care of
> integration with the platforms/desktops (Windows, Mac, Linux/Gnome,
> Linux/KDE and Solaris)
>

I second Ed's advice re: c++.  If you know what you're getting into,
then more power to you, but if you've never written a sizable app with
c++, then I strongly suggest looking at other languages.  C++ is very
popular because of momentum--any language will do what you want (they
are all "fast enough" performance-wise), and most of them will cause
less frustration than c++ :)

--Rogan

touchscreen.

Palm does have a repair page,

water damaged device.  My impression is that repairs can be pretty
expensive.

screens.  And a video of how to do-it-yourself repair.  That might be
dubious or a challenge but would be a last resort than replacing it.

From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Sun Jun 10 20:34:58 2007
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)

On Sun, 2007-06-10 at 17:13 -0700, Charles Sliger wrote:
> My Palm Treo 700P was given a ride through the washing machine. (you can't
> get good help these days)
> 
> I took it apart and dried it out.
> 
> It appears to function but can't be fully tested because the touch-screen no
> longer works.
> 
> You can see a mixture of water and detergent beneath the top membrane of the
> screen.
> 
> I couldn't see any way of opening the screen to clean it out.
>
> Anyone out there had any experience with this?
> 
> Is it possible to get a replacement screen?

Almost certainly.  I once replaced the screen in my Palm IIIci after I
cracked it and a couple months ago I took apart an already-broken Treo
600 and it looked like the screen was replaceable.  You will probably
need a Torx driver size T-5 or so; they are often sold as "cell phone
screwdrivers."  I think I eventually managed to find mine at Home Depot,
but only after looking in their tool section for way too long.

You can probably find information on the forums at <URL:
http://www.pdaphonehome.com/>, <URL:http://discussion.treocentral.com/>
and <URL:http://forum.treonauts.com/> , particularly disassembly
instructions and source for the replacement screen.

Wil

http://nakedape.cc/wiki/

I am in search of a utility that I have seen with my own eyes once, so

What I seek is a way to connect to the main :0 display of a linux host
with VNC.  It is the equivalent of using VNC to connect to a Solaris
or Windows box, neither of which have the concept of multiple X

Carlos Konstanski


From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Sun Jun 10 21:57:29 2007
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)

In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0706102206090.16513@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0706102206090.16513@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

On Sun, 2007-06-10 at 22:08 -0600, Carlos Konstanski wrote:
> I am in search of a utility that I have seen with my own eyes once, so
> I know it exists.  But I cannot find it for the life of me.
> 
> What I seek is a way to connect to the main :0 display of a linux host
> with VNC.  It is the equivalent of using VNC to connect to a Solaris
> or Windows box, neither of which have the concept of multiple X
> displays.
> 
> Thanks in advance for any help that may come my way.

There are several ways to do it.  "x11vnc" is a X server module; I think
it might be the fastest option but it probably doesn't play well with
OpenGL or Composite (but in my experience, none of them do); "vino" is
part of GNOME and KDE also has one, although I forget the name.  If you
are using something else, I'm sure there are others that are not built
with a desktop infrastructure.

Wil

Well ... I *think* x11vnc works on Gentoo AMD64. It's kinda slow,
though. But you can log on to box A, start up a desktop, type "x11vnc
-usepw" and it will let you connect to that desktop from box B as
"xxx.yyy.zzz:0" with VNCViewer (or krdc, or ...).

That said, I usually just start up a VNC server or an NX server on one
machine and VNC viewer or KRDC or NX client to it ... I don't *have* to
go right to the main client. So far, NX seems to be a good bit snappier
than the other options.


From rsteff at comcast.net  Mon Jun 11 06:41:35 2007
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Mon, 11 Jun 2007 06:41:35 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] OT: Cell Phone Resurrection: Palm Treo
In-Reply-To: <B0037325166@bct-mail.bctonline.com>
References: <B0037325166@bct-mail.bctonline.com>
Message-ID: <466D510F.4090206@comcast.net>

Charles Sliger wrote:

> My Palm Treo 700P was given a ride through the washing machine. (you can't
> get good help these days)
> 
> I took it apart and dried it out.

Sadly, it is probably too late. Once the circuitry gets wet, corrosion
sets in -- and continues to develop. You may not see it right away, but
eventually it will rear its ugly green head. I wouldn't put too much
money into trying to repair this one.

During one of my lives as a "consultant" I worked the service desk at
AT&T Wireless. My task was primarily to process warranty repairs and
commiserate with those who didn't have a warranty. About the only water
damage that was temporary was if the phone was powered off before being
dropped into the water, and if it was immediately fished out, opened up,
and dried with a blow dryer.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens

References: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0706110816500.14413@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <466D8FD4.30308@schluting.com>

On 6/11/07 8:21 AM, Rich Shepard wrote:
>   The linux connections on this thread are the use of jpilot for the
> desktop
> version of the PDA's data, and using the phone to connect to my network.
> 
>   My question for Charles and other Treo 700p users is what I need to use
> this phone as a wireless modem for my notebook. Not every place I travel
> has
> free WiFi access, and being able to use the smart-phone instead would be
> helpful.
> 

Assuming your laptop has bluetooth, it's trivial. Just set up a dialer
to dial #777 (Sprint) and it'll work. (On the phone's bluetooth
settings, you have to tell it to act as a modem, and at that point other
bluetooth functions are disabled)

Works perfectly, and with Sprint PCS you get unlimited data, so yay. I
use my 650 whenever I travel. SSH is a bit annoying, because of the
latency, but once you get used to it it's quite usable.

Before I had the 650, I used a 3rd party USB cable to do the same with
the treo 600.

 -Charlie

I've successfully used a Sprint Treo650 and Verizon 700P as a modem
using Bluetooth DUN.  As someone pointed out recently, Bluetooth
dongles for computers that don't have BT built-in are cheaper than the
funky cables carriers sell.

Caveat: I've only used the 700P from a Palm Foleo, not my laptop.  But it
should be easy enough to configure the laptop once I get 'round to it.

From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Mon Jun 11 13:26:14 2007
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)

Message-ID: <1181593575.24596.9.camel@spartacus.nakedape.priv>

On Mon, 2007-06-11 at 11:43 -0700, Rich Shepard wrote:

>    I don't believe my 3-year-old Sony Vaio has bluetooth. And, I use Verizon,
> not Sprint.

I USB Bluetooth dongle can be had for $10-$20; I don't know if it's
worthwhile or not, but I had to do work remotely a few weeks ago with a
company-supplied laptop and phone and there were times when the mass of
cables on the tiny coffee-shop table was hazardous.  It would have also
been nice to be able to put the phone higher in hopes of better
reception.

If you're with Verizon, though, I hope you have checked the costs of
their data service--it's absurdly expensive.  (I don't know about other
carriers.)  I use a dial-up account when I'm in a pinch, but it's
horribly slow (even for dial-up it's slow) and takes ages to actually
connect.  It's also sorta questionable whether those doing dial-up
should be charged for data rates (and may be surprised by in the
future).

You would probably get better help with this stuff on the forums I
posted links to in my response to Chaz.

Wil

The price cannot be as bad as QWorst.  You get a whole 135megs (yes MEGS) 
for $39.95 a month.  And that is the high volume service. At the lowest 
level you pay 2 cents a Kilobyte.  (They don't tell you the rates until 
after you get the pda phone.)

T-Mobile cleaims to have "unlimited service" for $20 a month.  I did not 
have the time to verify the rates.  (They may get you for higher per 
minute charges elsewhere.)

Another good comparison would be the average age of the phones offered. 
Another place Qworst will come in dead last.

I also had Verizon EVDO from Nov 2005, even when it was only 1xRTT in
Portland, and just barely worked with the mac.

After being a loyal customer, paying first $80/month for the first 15 months
or so, and $60/month until February, they booted me off (with 15 day warning
and no room for appeal) uncerimoniously when I exceeded the then-unpublished
Double Super Sekret limit of 5GB in a given month.  (I was in Buffalo for two
weeks, using 1xRTT to keep up to date on my few dozen podcasts.  Nothing
special.)

So, I walked across the street to the Sprint store, signed up for their
$60/month *truly* unlimited plan, and couldn't be happier.  For one, Sprint
has EVDO-A *everywhere*.  Verizon is EVDO-A only in a few select cities, and
*might* finish EVDO-A by the end of the year.  Oddly enough, Sprint customers
can *roam* to Verizon's towers free of charge, so it's not even a matter of
"coverage".

Ignore Verizon for being idiots, and losing my business.  Sprint is the winner
here.  Thank you Verizon for breaking my second 2-year contract 21 months
early, free of charge. :)

m0gely wrote:
> Use an email that is not associated with your actual name or domain
> name.  The account that comes with your ISP, or gmail/hotmail/yahoo
> should work.  If you hit up google for "m0gely" your going to know alot

The quick 'n dirty path to a sort-of-anonymous gmail account:

1. Drive to another part of town (be weary of CCTV at stoplights, maybe
use side-roads only)
2. Cnange the MAC address of your wireless NIC
3. Find an open/free AP
4. Use firefox tor plugin
5. Open a gmail account
6. Open a hotmail account
7. Send gmail invite to hotmail account
8. Open new gmail account
9. Rince-repeat with gmail invites and others (yahoo)
10. Once you have your final gmail account, only use tor to send/receive
email via gmail web interface (using only free/open AP's, but you could
also use home Internet if you trust tor enough)
10a. Make sure your cookie/cache cleaning is configured properly in firefox
10b. Use dm-crypt on your laptop, at least for /home

* Remember kids: A tinfoil hat has been tested by MIT to *amplify* radio
waves to your head. :]

I'm just a packet pusher.

From creswick at gmail.com  Wed Jun 13 12:05:14 2007
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Wed, 13 Jun 2007 12:05:14 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Possibly OT: Graph drawing tools for the web.
Message-ID: <c834ec80706131205g1a4483d6p28bcbfbac828c9d1@mail.gmail.com>

I need to build a site that (amongst other things) generates graphs
(node-and-link graphs).  Some of the features we'll need are:

* zooming / panning:  The graphs can be quite large, so viewing one
will not be a single-screen adventure, at least not at a level that
allows details of the nodes / links to be investigated.
* Node / link labeling:  The nodes / links need to have labels.
* hyperlinking: Nodes need to be hyperlinks (or something on the node
needs to be a hyperlink)
* automatic layout: The graphs are generated automatically, so they
will need to be laid out automatically as well.  There is no guarantee
that they will be planar.
* editable: This is not a high priority, but it would be really nice
of the nodes could be moved around and edges or nodes added / deleted.

All of this needs to happen in the browser, as far as the user is
concerned (I don't really care if it's server-side or client-side, but
it can not require any additional client-side software. So, I'm
assuming it'll need to be inherently Flash, Javascript, an applet, or
similar.)

Graphviz is the best looking option, since it generates svg and image
maps, but image maps don't fill many of the requirements, and I've no
idea how to display SVG in a browser.  Major props to any library /
solution that can be fed an xml representation of the graph and
hyperlinks. (Maybe I could just generate an svg version directly? but
how would it be displayed?)

aiSee (http://www.absint.com/aisee/ ) looks like it might do what I
need, but it is inherently a desktop app, and I'd really rather not
use a commercial solution if it can be avoided (although it is an
option).  JGraph is in about the same situation.

Does anyone have suggestions?  This is (unfortunately) for an ASP.Net
app, but I'd love to have (Yet Another) excuse to use a different web
technology ;).

Thanks,
Rogan

This is worth emphasizing: sometimes you really really want out of that
contract, and it's useful to have ways that are known to work.  

Perhaps there's a business opportunity here.  At my previous job I
wrote a little test app to gather stats on the performance -- latency,
bandwidth, etc. -- of the carriers we were targeting for a Palm email
client.  For a few days it had a bug such that it pumped out packets
at whatever the max the device was capable of.  I ran it for something
like 48 hours before noticing the level of traffic hitting the server.
I should package that app, bug and all, as VerizonOptOut, and post it
as shareware.  Or maybe the carriers would pay me not to post it.  :-)

More seriously, there should be a website listing ways to get out of
one-sided contracts.  For those with EVDO cards and linux laptops,
'ping -f' would probably be enough.

--Eric

Folks, 

There are four of us on the FreeGeek LPI study group list

So if you're interested and about ready to take an LPI exam, join the
list and let us know.

Thanks,
Mike

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Thu Jun 14 12:20:46 2007
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Thu, 14 Jun 2007 12:20:46 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] New xorg and laptops with external displays
Message-ID: <20070614192046.GA30409@gate.kl-ic.com>


I've installed whizzy new Scientific Linux 5, a Red Hat Linux 5 clone
that is a lot like Fedora Core 6.  It incorporates xorg 1.1.1-48 .

Unlike previous versions of X, this one makes full use of the dual
display potentialities of my laptop's mobile radeon chipset.  The
external display out the VGA connector in the back shows a completely
different "dual head" display than the laptop screen itself.  When
the right presentation software appears, this will be really cool -
I will be able to keep thumbnails on the laptop screen with a separate
display out the computer projector, for example.

But with 2007 presentation software, it is a pain in the butt.  I
would like the option to clone the laptop display to the VGA connector.

Is there any easy way to clone the display, to emulate the behavior
of the past?

This will become especially important when we do presentations at
PLUG meetings, as more and more semi-upgraded systems show up, with
the display on the laptop and blackness on the VGA connector, because
the dual head options are not properly set up.  

Keith

From vramnum10 at gmail.com  Thu Jun 14 14:54:27 2007
From: vramnum10 at gmail.com (User Iam)
Date: Thu, 14 Jun 2007 14:54:27 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] apache
Message-ID: <727fc2ee0706141454m3996d73p37b0eab2f309ae32@mail.gmail.com>

Does apache read the vhosts file on the fly or do I need to restart??


User Iam


From danielmyoung at gmail.com  Thu Jun 14 16:16:11 2007
From: danielmyoung at gmail.com (Dan Young)
Date: Thu, 14 Jun 2007 16:16:11 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] apache
In-Reply-To: <727fc2ee0706141454m3996d73p37b0eab2f309ae32@mail.gmail.com>
References: <727fc2ee0706141454m3996d73p37b0eab2f309ae32@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <2e42bd9b0706141616v6d0aec16h4af8b399138358d5@mail.gmail.com>

On 6/14/07, User Iam <vramnum10 at gmail.com> wrote:
> Does apache read the vhosts file on the fly or do I need to restart??

I believe a reload is required.

This should work regardless of distro:
apachectl configtest && killall -USR1 httpd

/etc/init.d/httpd configtest && /etc/init.d/httpd graceful
or in the Red Hat idiom:
service httpd configtest && service httpd graceful

I read a bit on this before responding, and it clarified for me the
behavior of the Red Hat initscript "reload" which merely sends a HUP
to httpd. I have frequently used this assuming this did not kill
running child processes. This doesn't seem to be the case according
to:
http://httpd.apache.org/docs/2.2/stopping.html#hup

Can anyone confirm?

-- 
Dan

From mikeraz at patch.com  Fri Jun 15 10:04:19 2007
From: mikeraz at patch.com (Michael Rasmussen)
Date: Fri, 15 Jun 2007 10:04:19 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] What is in a Name Server??
In-Reply-To: <e2aeccd60706142055h2bb15c58n26568e48d54a7d69@mail.gmail.com>
References: <727fc2ee0706141308q58ff31fen1ab19eaba3c1494@mail.gmail.com>
	<e2aeccd60706142055h2bb15c58n26568e48d54a7d69@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <28268.170.135.112.12.1181927059.squirrel@mail.patch.com>


drew wymore wrote:
> Nope doesn't matter although you can't use underscrores, only dots or
> periods.

Not true, kinda.  Legal characters for a host names are ASCII letters, digits and
the dash character. His ns1_server is not legal but the ns1-server construct would
be.

See http://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc1123.txt and
http://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc952.txt

I may have missed this in what you wrote above. Do you have
$user@'$theboxyourconnectingfrom' on the database server?

You would either need to grant a wildcard user or otherwise you have to add
a user for each hostname you would be connecting from.

Just re-read your above post. For the localhost issue you need to add a user
for $user at localhost instead of $user at 127.0.0.1

Let me know if that makes sense.

Then, I exited mysql.

Then, if I try 
mysql -h halibut
I cannot connect to the mysql server, even as root.

If I try (as non-root ted)
mysql auth -h halibut -u webauth at halibut -p
and give the password, I cannot authenticate. The error tells me that webauth at localhost cannot authenticate. 

If I grant all permisions to webauth at localhost (in mysql with the grant all command) I can authenticate (I try as non-root ted). But that's not what I wanted so I removed the localhost--webauth mysql user.

There is a halibut--webauth  mysql user in the user table for the default mysql database as shown below.

mysql> use mysql;
Database changed
mysql> select host,user from user;
+-----------+------------------+
| host      | user             |
+-----------+------------------+
| halibut   | root             |
| halibut   | webauth          |
| localhost | debian-sys-maint |
| localhost | root             |
+-----------+------------------+
4 rows in set (0.00 sec)

It appears that mysql does not recognize halibut.

My /etc/hosts has 
127.0.0.1       localhost
127.0.1.1       halibut 

But if I add the option --bind-address=127.0.1.1 to my mysql invocation as follows
/usr/bin/mysqld_safe --user=mysql --bind-address 127.0.1.1

then when I try
mysql auth -h halibut -u webauth -p
give the password, I get get in (as non-root ted).

Apparently one can also achieve this by editing the bind-address line in the file my.cnf which for my Ubuntu is in /etc/mysql. I installed mysql from the Synaptic Package Manager and this is where it put it. The option on the invocation line apparently overrides my.cnf. (which has bind-address = 127.0.0.1).

This is just hacking on my part. I'm unclear on what is actually happening. And I was posting here hoping that some experts might shed some light. I did what I did by cruising the mysql blogs and forums and reading sections in the mysql online manual.

So actually it's working the way I want, but I'm concerned about having a kooky unconventional system.

From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Sat Jun 16 11:59:50 2007
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Sat, 16 Jun 2007 11:59:50 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Trying to ssh
In-Reply-To: <191639738.1182016496451.JavaMail.root@fepweb07>
References: <191639738.1182016496451.JavaMail.root@fepweb07>
Message-ID: <200706161159.50366.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

# from tkubaska at charter.net
# on Saturday 16 June 2007 10:54 am:

>I'm trying to use ssh. I can ssh to other machines. But when I try to
> ssh to myself (actually I want other machines to ssh to me, but ths
> is a start) I get a connection refused. I even turned off FireStarter
> and still get this connection refused.

`ssh localhost` is potentially different than `ssh $yourmachine` from 
elsewhere depending on the ListenAddress in /etc/sshd_config.  Try 
doing `ssh $somemachine ssh $yourmachine hostname` and see what 
happens.  Assuming the absence of firewalls it should work.

AFAIK, the only way to get "Connection refused" as an answer is that the 
port is not open/listening.  That is, `telnet yourmachine 22` should 
give you

  Trying 127.0.0.1...
  Connected to localhost.
  Escape character is '^]'.
  SSH-2.0-OpenSSH_3.8p1 Debian 1:3.8p1-3

That's when you hit ctrl+c unless you have the ssh protocol memorized.  
If your daemon isn't listening, you'll get "Connection refused" from 
telnet too.

--Eric

well-mannered.

From david.fleck at mchsi.com  Sat Jun 16 15:29:39 2007
From: david.fleck at mchsi.com (David Fleck)
Date: Sat, 16 Jun 2007 17:29:39 -0500 (CDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Trying to ssh
In-Reply-To: <349646179.1182019682048.JavaMail.root@fepweb07>
References: <349646179.1182019682048.JavaMail.root@fepweb07>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0706161724260.14444@grond.sourballs.org>

On Sat, 16 Jun 2007, tkubaska at charter.net wrote:
> I attempted to enable port 22 in my router under Port Range Forward, but 
> still get the error. This is a generic LinkSys router.

You should be able to ssh to the machine you're currently on. It shouldn't 
inovle the router at all, just the local machine's tcp/ip stack.

What does the output of 'netstat -a | grep ssh' look like? On my machine, 
it's:

dcf>$ netstat -a | grep ssh
tcp        0      0 *:ssh                   *:*                     LISTEN      

If you don't have that, then sshd isn't running, and your machine can't 
talk to ssh clients.



--
David Fleck
david.fleck at mchsi.com

From ron at Opus1.COM  Sat Jun 16 14:53:23 2007
From: ron at Opus1.COM (Ronald Chmara)
Date: Sat, 16 Jun 2007 14:53:23 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Trying to ssh
In-Reply-To: <191639738.1182016496451.JavaMail.root@fepweb07>
References: <191639738.1182016496451.JavaMail.root@fepweb07>
Message-ID: <56663274-67FB-4D19-B38A-BBB68E9013C1@opus1.com>


On Jun 16, 2007, at 10:54 AM, tkubaska at charter.net wrote:

> I'm trying to use ssh. I can ssh to other machines. But when I try  
> to ssh to myself (actually I want other machines to ssh to me, but  
> ths is a start) I get a connection refused. I even turned off  
> FireStarter and still get this connection refused.
>
> ted at halibut:~$ ssh -l ted halibut
> ssh: connect to host halibut port 22: Connection refused
> ted at halibut:~$
>
> I replaced my hostname with my IP address and still get the error.  
> Clearly I haven't enabled something, but I've been searching for  
> what that is for the last few hours. Can someone point me in the  
> right direction? Thanks.
>  -ted


#Is sshd set to be enabled on start?
chkconfig | grep sshd

#Is sshd currently running?
/sbin/service sshd status
ps -elf | grep sshd

#is port 22 listening on your machine, regardless of the client?
telnet localhost 22

#what kind of connections are allowed system wide?
less /etc/ssh/sshd_config

other things to look into: what kind of connections are allowed for a  
given username (usually in .~/ssh/ ), whether or not sshd on your box  
has pam restrictions, etc... but this is a start...

-Bop


From keithl at kl-ic.com  Sat Jun 16 21:43:25 2007
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Sat, 16 Jun 2007 21:43:25 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] /etc/resolv.conf and DNS servers
Message-ID: <20070617044325.GC7376@gate.kl-ic.com>


This is a solution, not a question.  If you are setting up DNS
for your internal network, this might be useful to you.

The name server is the program that turns a text URL into an IP
address.  This is sometimes called DNS, domain name service.

I have a firewall that provides name service to the machines on
my internal network.  Outside, it connects to comcast.  After
migrating my firewall to a new distro, I was laboring under the
mistaken impression that my name server only knew about my own
addresses, and that my internal machines also needed access to
the external comcast name servers.  I was going nuts trying to
figure out how to write an /etc/resolv.conf file that had both my
internal name server and the comcast name server addresses in it.

This was a mistake.  The BIND named DNS server that comes with the
distro is designed to go straight to the root DNS servers, and then
to each domain server, and do all the name lookup itself, providing
an answer for the firewall machine and for the internal machines
without any need of the comcast dns server.  As long as the file
named.cache (or equivalent) is accurate, the local DNS server has
enough information to start the lookup process.  The most recent
update to the named.cache file was January 2004 - those root servers 
aren't going anywhere.  

So, the firewall machine's resolv.conf file should point only at the
internal server.  I hardwired the file, then did a chattr +i to make
it immutable, so some random process won't change it.  If the name
server fails, I do have a little bit of information in the file 
/etc/hosts ;  just enough to send a warning message to my internal
mail server.

Keith

Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993

> > of the past?

> There is, if you consider hacking your xorg.conf to be easy. I found
> this guide very helpful:
> 
>   <http://ozlabs.org/~jk/docs/mergefb/>
> 
> There may also be some whizbang KDE/GNOME way of getting there, too,
> but I'm not aware of one.

Actually, it turned out that the old xorg.conf worked with cloning,
/except/ that I had my laptop BIOS set incorrectly (the primary
display was set for the external "PCI" video, not the internal "AGP"
video.  On the older xorg servers, that was ignored, but the newer
xorg servers are more capable and can split the frame buffers, and do
so.  The post is good, because it pointed at some valuable information,
and clued me in to read the radeon(4) man page, which tells what all
the optional parameters do.

In early December 2006, MetroFi launched its Proof-of-Concept network.

From seniorr at aracnet.com  Mon Jun 18 00:01:34 2007
From: seniorr at aracnet.com (Russell Senior)
Date: 18 Jun 2007 00:01:34 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] End of an (uptime) era
Message-ID: <86odjdbvap.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>


This evening, the neighborhood had an extended power outage.  Not that
long really, but 5 or 10 minutes.  Long enough to outlast the aging
battery in the low-end UPS a couple of my computers were plugged into.
When the last trickle of AC power left the UPS, the machine I have
been reading/writing email and occasionally working on for 3+ years
without a reboot took a brief nap.

On March 11, 2004 I built a then-brand-spanking-new 2.4.25 kernel and
rebooted.  Until about 8:15 this evening, the machine, a dual-proc 500
MHz (slot 1) P3, had been running continuously ever since.  In the
meantime, an unused IDE drive had died.  A front-grill fan had seized,
but the box was bopping along just fine until mr electron and his
many, many friends decided to take a break from their 60 Hz dance for
a while.

I had just this afternoon bragged at the clinic to the person I was
helping about the massive uptime.  I guess I jinxed myself.  It makes
me sad, but there we are.  An opportunity to rejoin the 21st century
with a new 2.6 kernel.  The king is dead.  Long live the king.  Or
something.


-- 
Russell Senior         ``I have nine fingers; you have ten.''
seniorr at aracnet.com


From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Mon Jun 18 06:47:50 2007
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Mon, 18 Jun 2007 07:47:50 -0600 (MDT)
Subject: [PLUG] spam filtering: server vs. client
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0706180716020.20907@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>

My mailserver setup has spam filtering in place, but it has proven to
be inadequate.  Many messages are getting through the filter without
receiving any spam score whatsoever.  It is time to add bayes
filtering to the mix.

One can implement bayes filtering on the server, or on each client.
Server-side filtering is what the users want: a magical filter that
just works.  Client-side filtering puts the burden of filter training
on the users, but their filter is more acutely tailored to their
emails.

I envision a server-side solution with a small client-side twist.
Each user would have a folder called "spam" where they would put any
spam that makes it into their inbox.  The sa-learn job running on the
server would then look in each user's spam folder and learn those
messages as spam, and delete them when done.  In time, they would find
decreasing amounts of spam in their inbox, and their involvement in
the filter training would decrease as well.

The biggest potential problem with this method (or any server-side
method, for that matter) is that the filter is being trained on all
the users' spam.  It is not tailored for each individual.  There is
plenty of discussion on the subject of "one man's spam is another
man's ham" on the web.  My question is: is all this discussion merely
theoretical, or does it carry weight in the practical world?  Will my
users miss emails they really wanted to see if I train the filter on
all their spam as a whole?

There's also the question of ham.  Without ham, one cannot train a
spam filter.  Will I confuse the filter by using the ham from several
different users?  Or will the relevant tokens be discovered
regardless?

In short, I am tying to find a balance between theoretically correct
spam filtering, and practical filtering that does what it is supposed
to do: keep users from seeing spam in their inboxes.  This is the line
which I'm sure many of you have found.  Please share your thoughts.

Carlos Konstanski


From creswick at gmail.com  Mon Jun 18 10:13:47 2007

This is a Mac OS-X "dashboard" widget.  The latest versions of
CruiseControll also features a "dashboard" view, but the two things are
completely different.  (http://cruisecontrol.sourceforge.net/dashboard.html)

The ~/Library/ ... directory would exist if you were on a Mac, and it would
be in $HOME, as you suspected.

If you're not on a Mac, then you're SOL for the dashboard widget you linked
to, but the other dashboard view should "just work" (but it's just a
web-based thing).

From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)

Subject: [PLUG] 2.6.xx HAL automounting CD with cd volume name - yuk
Message-ID: <20070618174856.GA8780@gate.kl-ic.com>


Color me old-fashioned, but the new 2.6xx Hardware Abstraction Layer
(HAL) behavior of mounting a CDROM in /media using the CD's volume
name is annoying (and hard to write scripts for).  For example,  if
the CD is named "New Volume", it mounts as "/media/New Volume" (a
filename including a space).  

Here are some of the properties for HAL entry
 /org/freedesktop/Hal/devices/volume_label_New_Volume , extracted
with hal-get-property :

info.product                  : New Volume
volume.label                  : New Volume
volume.mount_point            : /media/New Volume
volume.fstype                 : iso9660
linux.hotplug_type            : 3
block.device                  : /dev/hdc
block.storage_device          : /org/freedesktop/Hal/devices/storage_model_TOSHIBA_DVD_ROM_SD_R2002

Is there something I can tweak so that the CD on /dev/cdrom always
mounts as /media/cdrom or /mnt/cdrom ?  

Keith

In-Reply-To: <28268.170.135.112.12.1181927059.squirrel@mail.patch.com>
References: <727fc2ee0706141308q58ff31fen1ab19eaba3c1494@mail.gmail.com>	<e2aeccd60706142055h2bb15c58n26568e48d54a7d69@mail.gmail.com>

Michael Rasmussen wrote:
> drew wymore wrote:
>> Nope doesn't matter although you can't use underscrores, only dots or
>> periods.
> 
> Not true, kinda.  Legal characters for a host names are ASCII letters, digits and
> the dash character. His ns1_server is not legal but the ns1-server construct would
> be.
> 
> See http://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc1123.txt and
> http://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc952.txt


There's at least one DNS-related RFCs (I've forgotten
which one) that says "any binary pattern" is allowable
in a DNS name part but, other than Microsoft, nobody
supports this in DNS software. Even the IDNA
(Internationalized domain names) folks use algorithms
that use punycode to ensure that name parts use only
letters, numbers, and the hyphen (dash). Still, it's
possible for people to claim, as Microsoft apparently
does, that any characters are possible in name parts.

Ed Sawicki

Message-ID: <1d065ed40706181130h28360d4emc96a8fa47397993a@mail.gmail.com>

On 6/18/07, Ed Sawicki <ed at alcpress.com> wrote:
> Michael Rasmussen wrote:
> > drew wymore wrote:
> >> Nope doesn't matter although you can't use underscrores, only dots or
> >> periods.
> >
> > Not true, kinda.  Legal characters for a host names are ASCII letters, digits and
> > the dash character. His ns1_server is not legal but the ns1-server construct would
> > be.
> >
> > See http://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc1123.txt and
> > http://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc952.txt
>
>
> There's at least one DNS-related RFCs (I've forgotten
> which one) that says "any binary pattern" is allowable
> in a DNS name part but, other than Microsoft, nobody
> supports this in DNS software. Even the IDNA
> (Internationalized domain names) folks use algorithms
> that use punycode to ensure that name parts use only
> letters, numbers, and the hyphen (dash). Still, it's
> possible for people to claim, as Microsoft apparently
> does, that any characters are possible in name parts.
>
> Ed Sawicki

It's RFC 2181, http://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2181.txt ,
"Clarifications to the DNS Specification".

According to RFC 2181, while you can put any binary up to 63 octets
into a label, that doesn't mean that there aren't other restrictions.
For example:

- SMTP won't allow arbitrary binary in specifying a host for mail delivery
- Registries won't allow arbitrary binary in domain names, nor
probably in NS record glue
- Clients may generally puke

So, in theory, you can name your host e=mc^2.example.com, but there's
no guarantee that anyone else in the world will ever be able to reach
it.

-A

On Mon, Jun 18, 2007 at 10:48:56AM -0700, Keith Lofstrom wrote:
> 
> Color me old-fashioned, but the new 2.6xx Hardware Abstraction Layer
> (HAL) behavior of mounting a CDROM in /media using the CD's volume
> name is annoying (and hard to write scripts for).  For example,  if
> the CD is named "New Volume", it mounts as "/media/New Volume" (a
> filename including a space).  
> 
> Here are some of the properties for HAL entry
>  /org/freedesktop/Hal/devices/volume_label_New_Volume , extracted
> with hal-get-property :
> 
> info.product                  : New Volume
> volume.label                  : New Volume
> volume.mount_point            : /media/New Volume
> volume.fstype                 : iso9660
> linux.hotplug_type            : 3
> block.device                  : /dev/hdc
> block.storage_device          : /org/freedesktop/Hal/devices/storage_model_TOSHIBA_DVD_ROM_SD_R2002
> 
> Is there something I can tweak so that the CD on /dev/cdrom always
> mounts as /media/cdrom or /mnt/cdrom ?  
> 
> Keith

I have learned more.  The automounting does not occur when my machine
is running level 3.  This is actually something that gnome (specifically
gnome-volume-manager) does in cooperation wuth HAL, so I can turn off
the automounting with :

 gnome -> System -> Preferences -> Removeable Drives and Media

And there are no options besides turning media automount on and off,
none that I can find with the configuration editor, either.  Fooey.
I just turned it off, and built some shell scripts to do it (and
sudo'd mount, umount, and eject so I can drive them as a user).

Keith

From tkubaska at charter.net  Mon Jun 18 22:54:35 2007
From: tkubaska at charter.net (Ted Kubaska)

Subject: [PLUG] can access an intranet site with Linux but not with Windows?
Message-ID: <1182232475.16714.49.camel@halibut>

Here's a curious Linux/Windows thing that is troubling me. I posted a
similar question on the .Net list, but discussions that have Linux in
them often remain quiet there.

I can access a site with Linux and not with Windows. Is there something
in my Windows configuration that's preventing this? I don't know where
to look.  (I temporarily turned off my Windows firewall and see the same
problem.)

One of the machines in my local network is a Linux box. On that machine
I have apache that serves up a site. I can access this site from that
same Linux box. And I can access it from another Linux box on my local
network. I put http://192.168.1.100/phpinfo.php in my browser, and see
what I expect.

However, if I am on a Windows XP box on my local network and do the
same (that is access from Windows the site on my local Linux box), I get
"Internet Explorer cannot display the webpage." I see the
same problem with Firefox.

Does anyone know what there is in Windows that is preventing this
access?
-ted



From ogmoid at gmail.com  Mon Jun 18 23:07:58 2007

On Mon, Jun 18, 2007 at 10:45:56PM -0700, Ted Kubaska wrote:
> What do you guys use for remote access? 
> 
> I want to see a remote desktop locally. I tried out XDMCP which I read
> has security issues? It works fine otherwise. Other possibilities are
> tightvnc and realvnc (which I have not tried). I want to see a remote

NX. Far and away the best I've encountered.

> Anyway if you do use remote desktops, what tools have you had good
> results with? Thanks.

Any -> Linux    : NX
Any -> Windows  : RDP
Any -> Mac      : VNC

NX
clients: http://www.nomachine.com/
linux remote: http://freenx.berlios.de/

RDP
linux client: http://www.rdesktop.org/

VNC
linux client: http://www.tightvnc.com/

From tkubaska at charter.net  Tue Jun 19 09:19:02 2007
From: tkubaska at charter.net (TedK)
Date: Tue, 19 Jun 2007 09:19:02 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] can access an intranet site with Linux but
	not	with	Windows?
In-Reply-To: <4677B8C7.9060504@frankhunt.com>
References: <1182232475.16714.49.camel@halibut>	<1182236403.16714.53.camel@halibut>
	<4677B8C7.9060504@frankhunt.com>
Message-ID: <001501c7b28d$8d1c8d60$a755a820$@net>

Thanks for responding. It turned out that the problem was that Firestarter
was not accepting connections from my Windows box ... don't know if this was
the right thing to do but what I did was open up Firestarter, choose the
Policy tab and under Allow Connections from Host, added the ip address of my
local Windows. The reason the connection worked from another Linux ox was
that the ip address of the Linux box was already there. BTW my Linux box is
a virtual Linux running under VMware on my Windows box. When the problem
occurred, it occurred for both IE and Firefox. So now it works with
FIrestarter running.
 -ted

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Tue Jun 19 10:51:30 2007
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Tue, 19 Jun 2007 10:51:30 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] mutt (or other text mail reader), html, and w3m
Message-ID: <20070619175130.GC16104@gate.kl-ic.com>


OK, I am one of those ancient fossils who hates html email, which is
the spawn of Satan and his evil minions.   It is distracting, a path
for viruses to attack fragile html viewers, incompatable with some
ssh tunnels, and included files like graphics break privacy when they
are uploaded.

In order to read html email with fewer risks, I use w3m, which is
included in my distro (Scientific Linux 5).  w3m presents the html
as formatted ascii text.  It can be made to download graphics and
other inclusions, but I leave that nonsense turned off.

I had forgotten how to configure it when I upgraded my mail server
from Redhat-Prehistoric to SL5.  For those of you who have also
forgotten, you edit /etc/mailcap:

### text/html; /usr/bin/htmlview %s ; copiousoutput
text/html; /usr/bin/w3m -T text/html %s ; copiousoutput

Now html email shows up as text in your text email browser (I use
mutt, but this probably also works in elm and pine).

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

Most current email clients will give the user a choice of receiving  
email as HTML or plain text. I also prefer plain text email. I use  
Evolution for email and have it set to send/receive email as plain text.

-Ken

> from Redhat-Prehistoric to SL5.  For those of you who have also
> forgotten, you edit /etc/mailcap:
>
> ### text/html; /usr/bin/htmlview %s ; copiousoutput
> text/html; /usr/bin/w3m -T text/html %s ; copiousoutput
>
> Now html email shows up as text in your text email browser (I use
> mutt, but this probably also works in elm and pine).

On Tue, 19 Jun 2007, Rich Shepard wrote:

> On Tue, 19 Jun 2007, Keith Lofstrom wrote:

>>  is the spawn of Satan and his evil minions.

>  I, too, am an older curmudgeon. I have pine set to translate html 
> messages to plain ASCII text. Most of the time it Just Works; when 
> it doesn't, I get the usualy mess of tags and text and usually 
> ignore it all by pressing the 'd' key.

A slightly less-old curmudgeon :-), I use alpine -- which is, in 
effect, Pine 5.0 with a much less restrictive license (the Apache 
license, to be exact). It uses libxml2 to handle HTML, and does so 
semi-well: text formatting and links decently, tables not so well.

For me, the big selling point in moving from Pine to Alpine is Unicode 
support. I want to read my spam in the original 
Chinese/Hebrew/Russian, thank you very much! Still no integrated GPG 
support, though, which is a fairly major bummer.

From ali.corbin at gmail.com  Tue Jun 19 12:07:44 2007
From: ali.corbin at gmail.com (Ali Corbin)
Date: Tue, 19 Jun 2007 12:07:44 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] mutt (or other text mail reader), html, and w3m
In-Reply-To: <20070619175130.GC16104@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <20070619175130.GC16104@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <965f90c20706191207o446207d6lf4e3efb1bd298a93@mail.gmail.com>

On 6/19/07, Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com> wrote:
>
> I had forgotten how to configure it when I upgraded my mail server
> from Redhat-Prehistoric to SL5.  For those of you who have also
> forgotten, you edit /etc/mailcap:
>
> ### text/html; /usr/bin/htmlview %s ; copiousoutput
> text/html; /usr/bin/w3m -T text/html %s ; copiousoutput
>

I'll see your html and raise you a pdf and an msword:

text/html; /usr/bin/links %s ; copiousoutput
application/pdf; pdftotext %s - ; copiousoutput
application/msword; antiword %s ; copiousoutput

And when all else fails, mutt.octet.filter.pl will try to figure out
what the attachment really is and display it inline.

application/octet-stream;  mutt.octet.filter.pl %s; copiousoutput

(This is my set-up for work, where people send all sorts of silly
files in email.)

Ali

> from Redhat-Prehistoric to SL5.  For those of you who have also

works...

text/html; /usr/bin/lynx -dump -force_html '%s'; copiousoutput; description=HTML Text; nametemplate=%s.html

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Tue Jun 19 12:47:05 2007
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)

Subject: [PLUG] strange ln -s behavior

For about a 15 minute period, I was having the damnedest time making
a simple symbolic link.  I had just downloaded the Citrix client for
Linux, so my wife could access some records at a partner's site.  I
wanted to link the Citrix plugin into firefox:

  cd /opt/firefox/plugins
  ln -s /usr/lib/ICAClient/npica.so npica.so

All pretty standard, right?  When I run the ln command, I get:

  ln: accessing `?s': No such file or directory

WTF?  Many combinations of ln command later ( /bin/ln, --symbolic,
copying /bin/ln from another machine in case it is corrupted, etc.),
I am getting similar results (sometimes a hard link shows up).  I
am able to make symbolic links elsewhere.  I finally made a symbolic
link in /usr/lib/ICAClient/ and moved the link.  That worked.

Of course, by that time my wife had left for work.  She is a nice
person, so I didn't hear any mutterings about Linux.  At least 
from her.

And Citrix "works", BTW.  Evil windows polluting her laptop.  I
feel unclean.

I took a break to beat my head against the wall.  When I came back,
I temporarily moved the successful link, and did the ln -s command
again.  With command line repeat, no retyping.  It worked just fine. 

WTF????

I suspect evil devils from hell.  Or angels protecting my wife from
windows.  They finally gave up.  Any other explanations?  

Keith

From znmeb at cesmail.net  Tue Jun 19 18:54:44 2007
From: znmeb at cesmail.net (M. Edward (Ed) Borasky)
Date: Tue, 19 Jun 2007 18:54:44 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] remote Linux desktops
In-Reply-To: <1182231957.16714.41.camel@halibut>
References: <1182231957.16714.41.camel@halibut>
Message-ID: <467888E4.40907@cesmail.net>

Ted Kubaska wrote:
> What do you guys use for remote access? 
> 
> I want to see a remote desktop locally. I tried out XDMCP which I read
> has security issues? It works fine otherwise. Other possibilities are
> tightvnc and realvnc (which I have not tried). I want to see a remote
> Linux desktop on both local Windows and local Linux boxes. Suse docs
> recommend realvnc on a Windows box talking to a remote Linux box running
> tightvnc (strange combination I thought).
> 
> Anyway if you do use remote desktops, what tools have you had good
> results with? Thanks.
>  -ted
> 
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug
> 

Well ... here goes:

1. Windows server, Windows client: Microsoft's latest RDC.
2. Windows server, Linux client: either rdesktop or krdc. There are
others, but these two work best for me.
3. Linux server, insecure but free as in speech: all versions of vnc as
far as I can tell. This includes vnc, tightvnc and x11vnc. RealVNC is
the only free as in speech Windows client I'm aware of.
4. Linux server, secure but free as in beer: NX from NoMachines.com
5. Linux server, secure and free as in speech: freenx.

What do I use? Talking to a Windows box from Linux: rdesktop. krdc will
work as either a vnc or RDP client, but since I stopped running vnc
servers on my Linux boxes, I've gone back to rdesktop.

Talking to a Linux box from Windows: freenx server on the Linux box, the
free as in beer NxClient for Windows on the Windows box

Talking to a Linux box from Linux: freenx server as above, the free as
in beer NXClient for Linux on the client.

Why did I stop using VNC? I had some problems with both "vnc" and
"tightvnc". Some of the server apps were crashing looking for libraries
with the vnc server but ran fine on the server's desktop. And with the
tightvnc server, I couldn't get all the screen sizes right -- for some
reason I could only get 1024x768 and gave up trying to get past this.

Keith,

If an alias for "ln" had been set, your binary would be as you expect,
But you would be running something else.
If this happens again, try "unalias ln" to see if the behavior changes.

Question: Had you been setting aliases for "ls" and miskeyed?

> sets in -- and continues to develop. You may not see it right away, but

> money into trying to repair this one.

> During one of my lives as a "consultant" I worked the service desk at
> AT&T Wireless. My task was primarily to process warranty repairs and
> commiserate with those who didn't have a warranty. About the only water
> damage that was temporary was if the phone was powered off before being
> dropped into the water, and if it was immediately fished out, opened up,
> and dried with a blow dryer.

From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Thu Jun 21 03:34:13 2007
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Thu, 21 Jun 2007 03:34:13 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Re: help!  make usb keyboard stop working
In-Reply-To: <200706191345.38736.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
References: <200706191345.38736.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
Message-ID: <200706210334.13739.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

# from Eric Wilhelm
# on Tuesday 19 June 2007 01:45 pm:

>I can easily find the opposite answer, the problem that I have is that
> I want to plug in a usb keyboard (actually a magstripe reader (and a
> numeric keypad)) and have it *not* connect to the standard usb
> keyboard interface (I still need to be able to get data from it,
> though raw scancodes are fine.)

Answer:  libhid.  Now with sweet Perl pseudo-keyboard driver.

  http://scratchcomputing.com/svn/Linux-USBKeyboard/trunk

Once you call hid_force_open(), the kernel hid driver lets go of it and 
you can attach it to any daemon, etc.  I did have to map the scancodes 
to keycodes (and then to keys), but for magstripe (credit card) and 
barcode readers, you don't want to apply the dvorak keymap anyway :-D

--Eric
-- 
The first rule about Debian is you don't talk about Debian
---------------------------------------------------
    http://scratchcomputing.com

From merlyn at stonehenge.com  Thu Jun 21 08:23:45 2007
From: merlyn at stonehenge.com (Randal L. Schwartz)
Date: Thu, 21 Jun 2007 08:23:45 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Re: strange ln -s behavior
References: <20070619194705.GA16739@gate.kl-ic.com>
	<e2aeccd60706191250n1dc11a15gcb5731239f78ab1c@mail.gmail.com>
	<20070620134252.GA20859@gate.kl-ic.com>
	<014f01c7b351$76f9be30$6d01a8c0@RAMA>
	<c834ec80706201915m5742a87bt2c6eb917679e2d0e@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <86myytfi0u.fsf@blue.stonehenge.com>

>>>>> "Rogan" == Rogan Creswick <creswick at gmail.com> writes:

Rogan> In bash you can also prepend a command with a "\" to "unalias" it just
Rogan> once.  eg:

Rogan> $ \ls --color=always

But the proper answer is
NEVER NEVER NEVER OVERLOAD BUILT IN COMMANDS.

You want an "rm" that moves something to the trash?  Fine.  Call
it "del".  Don't make "rm" do that.  That way, if you're on a machine
that doesn't have your "del" alias, you know it immediately, instead
of invoking rm, wanting to recover, and then finding out that it's
"oh no!" the *real* rm.

*And* you don't run into problems like this, with "ln" not really meaning the
textbook "ln".  Feh.

I don't know why this is a hard concept to understand for people.  Maybe
they've just seen too many bad examples over the years.

--

<merlyn at stonehenge.com> <URL:http://www.stonehenge.com/merlyn/>
Perl/Unix/security consulting, Technical writing, Comedy, etc. etc.
See PerlTraining.Stonehenge.com for onsite and open-enrollment Perl training!

From johnxj at comcast.net  Thu Jun 21 11:12:05 2007
From: johnxj at comcast.net (John Jason Jordan)
Date: Thu, 21 Jun 2007 11:12:05 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Mouse click crashes X (I think)
Message-ID: <20070621111205.d26170fc.johnxj@comcast.net>

Ubuntu Feisty amd64, completely up to date
Compaq R3240 laptop, nVidia GeForce 4, plenty of free disk space, 1.25 GB RAM.
Logitech USB wireless notebook mouse

For a long time I have had a problem of getting suddenly logged out. That is, I assumed I was being logged out, but now I think it's really just X crashing and restarting. The reason I now think X is crashing is because occasionally I see a bit of command line just before the GUI login screen comes back up. Usually it's too fast to see any command line text, although the screen does go black for a moment before the login screen comes back up. When I do see text it is too fast to read it. It looks the same as if I press Ctrl-Alt-Bksp.

This started happening after upgrading to Edgy last December, and continues under Feisty. If I am using the computer all day long it will happen probably once during the day. It never happens as a result of keyboard input. The trigger is always a regular left mouse click. 

It happens most often in Firefox, but that's probably because Firefox is where I use the mouse a lot. It also seems that the more tabs I have open and the more other programs I have running, the more likely it is to happen. Yet, it has been known to happen even when Firefox is the only program running and I have only one tab open. It also happens with other programs besides Firefox, some more so than others. I have one small program used for testing language skills with children (Bubble Dialogue) running under Crossover Office and it will crash X within 30 minutes, unless I never use the mouse. However, I can't recall it ever happening with other programs that I use under Crossover Office. It is rare for it to happen with OpenOffice.org and I don't think I've ever had it happen with Sylpheed (mail client). The point is that I cannot come up with a pattern for when it happens that would lead to a diagnosis. I'd be thrilled if it was just one program, or just one kind of windo!
 w item I was clicking on -- anything that would give me a clue.

I prefer the nVidia driver, but switching to the nv driver makes no difference. Desktop is Gnome 2.18.1, 4/11/2007.

The computer does not have a port for a wired mouse, so my only options for testing are other USB mice, of which I have none. The built-in touchpad is Synaptic and it loads during boot and works fine, but it has a physical on-off switch and I always leave it turned off. I am unable to use the touchpad effectively due to poor finger motor control (you should see what I pass off as handwriting). I use the touchpad only for emergencies when I left the mouse at home or its batteries died. 

It is definitely not a random keypress, as it can happen when I am using the mouse and my other hand is resting in my lap.

After it happens and I log back in again I have run dmesg and found nothing unusual.

I have spent hours googling and have turned up only one post from 2005 with two responses from others, neither of which offered a solution, and no followup from the original poster. I posted about a month ago on Ubuntu forums, but got no response.

I have been trying different things since last December, but so far have not even been able to figure out what is causing it, let alone how to fix it. I'm out of ideas, so maybe someone can give me a fresh direction to look for the answer. All suggestions welcome.

> Ubuntu Feisty amd64, completely up to date

<snip problem description>

It's been my experience that weird semi-inexplicable problems are more often
than not rooted in hardware. What you describe sounds an awful lot like
dodgy RAM. I'd suggest running the memtest86 that ubuntu includes in the
grub menu overnight (or longer) to at least rule it out as a suspect.

I was having similar chronic computer crashiness some months ago. I gave the
RAM a good thorough test, and after running for about 12 hours, one of the
modules started throwing errors. Got it replaced under warranty, and I
haven't had a problem since.

I've seen similar situations play out that way a number of times.
-- 
-Regards-

-Quentin Hartman-

I found several files in /var/log, although they are named Xorg.n.log. I opened the one with the most recent timestamp, which was yesterday at about the time I logged back in again after a reboot. Unfortunately, it is long and I don't understand much of what is in it. It would take a month of studying how X works to figure out what all the lines mean. I don't see anything relating to the crash. The previous one does not help either because it says a the end "Fatal server error: no screens found." That is because I tried a suggestion I found elsewhere to use "pci=assign-busses" and the result was that X wouldn't start.

I did notice a bunch of stuff related to Wacom, ending with "unable to find device." I noted this because I have seen that in dmesg as well. For some reason Ubuntu thinks I have a Wacom tablet, even though there has never been one near this computer. I have been seeing messages relating to Wacom during the boot process since at least Dapper, probably forever. It may not be the source of the problem, but if I don't have a Wacom tablet I should figure out how to make the boot process stop trying to load a driver for it. I mean, just on general principles.

As for the mouse, there are several references in the Xorg.0.log file to the Synaptics touchpad and it seems to be loaded properly. (Of course it is loaded, it works! Duh!) However, the only reference I see to anything else is a line that includes "Explorer PS/2." (The boot process does mention Logitech, however.) So that makes me think that X is taking the external mouse input as though it is the Synaptics touchpad.

> I have several USB meese of which you're welcome to have one just let me
> know how/where/when to get it to you.

I may take you up on that. But I know the problem is not mechanical with the mouse, because the mouse I am using right now is the third that I have bought. I dropped the first one and broke it, and the scroll wheel failed on the second one. The current one is brand new, but the problem happened with all three. Since it is a Logitech, to test things properly I assume I should try a brand that uses a different driver.

I also take to heart your comment about the USB bits. I have long had a problem making backups to external USB drives. Usually it goes OK, but frequently I will get lockups. Happens whether I use tar, rsync, dar or just a plan cp command. So I assumed the problem has something to do with extended continuous data transfers over the USB ports. I've never gotten to the bottom of the problem. I just make backups now to another Linux PC using nfs. 

(Interscript: the computer I make backups to over nfs is the computer with the evil Abit board. I recently gave up on it, took it back to Fry's and swapped it for an Asus. Haven't reassembled the computer yet. Stay tuned.)

Re Quentin's suggestion on the RAM. It is a good suggestion, but dodgy RAM should also cause miscellaneous other nefarious things to happen, and I have no other such problems. However, the computer came with two 256 meg SODIMMs and I replaced one with a 1 GB SODIMM. They are different brands and different sizes. Theoretically, that should make no difference. But we all know how theories work. Hence, when I go to bed this evening I will reboot it with memtest and run it all night at least.

Re Kenneth's suggestion that it is the driver, I have to put the driver at the bottom of the list of possibilities. This is, after all, a Logitech mouse. If the Logitech driver was defective, even the amd64 version, the screaming would be melting internet connections worldwide. Having said that, it is very possible that I am loading the *wrong* driver. I guess I need to research which driver I am supposed to be using.

Thanks for the suggestions.

Subject: [PLUG] Multiple USB Ports Active On One Connection
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0706220605460.29781@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

   I bought a Treo 700p yesterday and am trying to restore the PDA databases
from jpilot on the desktop. However, when I plug in the USB cable to the
front of the machine, /var/log/messages shows it attached to both
ttyUSB0 and ttyUSB1:

Jun 22 05:59:30 salmo kernel: usb 1-4: new full speed USB device using
ohci_hcd and address 17
Jun 22 05:59:30 salmo kernel: usb 1-4: configuration #1 chosen from 1 choice
Jun 22 05:59:30 salmo kernel: visor 1-4:1.0: Handspring Visor / Palm OS
converter detected
Jun 22 05:59:30 salmo kernel: usb 1-4: Handspring Visor / Palm OS converter
now attached to ttyUSB0
Jun 22 05:59:30 salmo kernel: usb 1-4: Handspring Visor / Palm OS converter
now attached to ttyUSB1

   Never before have I seen this.

   There is no /dev/ttyUSBn, but there is /dev/tts/USB0 and /dev/tts/USB1.
Also, in /etc/udev/rules.d/udev.rules, there is the line,

KERNEL="ttyUSB[0-9]*",  NAME="tts/USB%n", GROUP="tty", MODE="0660"

   It was suggested to me by David Desrosiers, the author of pilot-link, that
I change the KERNEL value to "tts/USB[0-9]*", but that made no difference.

   I'd really appreciate an explanation of what's going on and what I should
do to get a connection on only a single port so I can restore data to the
PDA.

TIA,

Rich
